scope="row">President of Baseball Operations</th><td>\nMike Rizzo</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Washington Nationals</b> are a professional baseball team based in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>. The Nationals compete in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB) as a member club of the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> (NL) <a href="/wiki/National_League_East" title="National League East">East</a> division. From 2005 to 2007, the team played in <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy_Memorial_Stadium" title="Robert F. Kennedy Memorial Stadium">RFK Stadium</a>; since 2008 their home stadium has been <a href="/wiki/Nationals_Park" title="Nationals Park">Nationals Park</a> on <a href="/wiki/South_Capitol_Street" title="South Capitol Street">South Capitol Street</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southeast,_Washington,_D.C." title="Southeast, Washington, D.C.">Southeast D.C.</a>, near the <a href="/wiki/Anacostia_River" title="Anacostia River">Anacostia River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Nationals are <a href="/wiki/History_of_Washington,_D.C._professional_baseball" title="History of Washington, D.C. professional baseball">the eighth major league franchise to be based in Washington, D.C.</a>, and the first since 1971. The current National League club was founded in 1969 as the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/1969_Major_League_Baseball_expansion" title="1969 Major League Baseball expansion">MLB expansion</a>.  The Expos were purchased by Major League Baseball in 2002,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and the team was renamed the Nationals and moved to Washington, D.C. before the 2005 season, marking the first franchise relocation in MLB since the third Washington Senators moved to Texas in 1971.\n</p><p>While the team initially struggled after moving to Washington, the Nationals have experienced considerable success in recent years, winning division titles in 2012, 2014, 2016, and 2017, although they have yet to advance out of the first round in the playoffs.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Two of the team\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_first_overall_Major_League_Baseball_draft_picks" title="List of first overall Major League Baseball draft picks">first overall picks</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_draft" title="Major League Baseball draft">MLB Draft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Strasburg" title="Stephen Strasburg">Stephen Strasburg</a> in 2009 and <a href="/wiki/Bryce_Harper" title="Bryce Harper">Bryce Harper</a> in 2010, attracted new levels of attention to the team. At the time of his selection, Strasburg was called the "most-hyped pick in draft history," and Harper later became the youngest position player to be selected to the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="Major League Baseball All-Star Game">MLB All-Star Game</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Including their time in Montreal, the Nationals are one of two franchises, and the only one in the National League, never to have won a league pennant and played in a <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a>, along with the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Seattle Mariners</a> of the American League.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-World_Series_Club_History_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Series_Club_History-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" href="#Baseball_Hall_of_Famers"><span class="tocnumber">3.4</span> <span class="toctext">Baseball Hall of Famers</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Ford_C._Frick_Award"><span class="tocnumber">3.5</span> <span class="toctext">Ford C. Frick Award</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Retired_numbers"><span class="tocnumber">3.6</span> <span class="toctext">Retired numbers</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Ring_of_Honor"><span class="tocnumber">3.7</span> <span class="toctext">Ring of Honor</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Attendance_and_fans"><span class="tocnumber">3.8</span> <span class="toctext">Attendance and fans</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-19"><a href="#Attendance"><span class="tocnumber">3.8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Attendance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20"><a href="#Prominent_fans"><span class="tocnumber">3.8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Prominent fans</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Season_standings"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Season standings</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Spring_training"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Spring training</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Minor_league_affiliations"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Minor league affiliations</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Former_affiliates"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Former affiliates</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Nationals_Dream_Foundation"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Nationals Dream Foundation</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Radio_and_television"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Radio and television</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Rivalries"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Rivalries</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Baltimore_Orioles_(Beltway_Series)"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Baltimore Orioles (Beltway Series)</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Footnotes"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Footnotes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="Early_Baseball_in_Washington.2C_DC"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Baseball_in_Washington,_DC">Early Baseball in Washington, DC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early Baseball in Washington, DC">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Washington,_D.C._professional_baseball" title="History of Washington, D.C. professional baseball">History of Washington, D.C. professional baseball</a></div>\n<p>Multiple short-lived baseball franchises, including two named the Nationals, played in Washington with the National Association in the 1870s.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;note 1&#93;</a></sup> The first Washington Nationals team in a major league played in the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_(19th_century)" title="American Association (19th century)">American Association</a> in 1884.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>  Another Washington Nationals team also played in the <a href="/wiki/Union_Association" title="Union Association">Union Association</a> during its only season in 1884.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The first Washington Nationals of the National League played from 1886 to 1889.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>  \n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Washington_Senators">Washington Senators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Washington Senators">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Washington_Senators_(1891%E2%80%9399)" title="Washington Senators (1891\xe2\x80\x9399)">Washington Senators (1891\xe2\x80\x9399)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_Senators_(1912)" title="Washington Senators (1912)">Washington Senators (1912)</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Washington_Senators_(1901%E2%80%9360)" title="History of the Washington Senators (1901\xe2\x80\x9360)">History of the Washington Senators (1901\xe2\x80\x9360)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers (baseball)</a></div>\n<p>The Washington Statesmen played in the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_(19th_century)" title="American Association (19th century)">American Association</a> in 1891,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> before jumping to the National League as the Senators the following season.  The <a href="/wiki/Washington_Senators_(1891%E2%80%9399)" title="Washington Senators (1891\xe2\x80\x9399)">Washington Senators</a>, who were often referred to as the Nationals,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> played in the National League from 1892 to 1899. They were followed by another <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Washington_Senators_(1901%E2%80%9360)" title="History of the Washington Senators (1901\xe2\x80\x9360)">Washington Senators</a> franchise in 1901, a charter member of the new <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a>, who were officially named the Washington Nationals from 1905 to 1956. The first American League Senators franchise moved to Minnesota in 1961 and became the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Minnesota Twins</a>. They were replaced that season by a <a href="/wiki/Washington_Senators_(1961%E2%80%9371)" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Senators (1961\xe2\x80\x9371)">second Senators franchise</a>, who eventually moved to <a href="/wiki/Arlington,_Texas" title="Arlington, Texas">Arlington, Texas</a>, after the 1971 season and became the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a>.\n</p><p><br />\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Montreal_Expos">Montreal Expos</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Montreal Expos">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/1969_Major_League_Baseball_expansion" title="1969 Major League Baseball expansion">MLB expansion</a>, which included the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Pilots" title="Seattle Pilots">Seattle Pilots</a> (now the Milwaukee Brewers),<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a>, and <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a>. Based in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, the Expos were the first Major League team in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The majority-share owner was by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Bronfman" title="Charles Bronfman">Charles Bronfman</a>, a major shareholder in <a href="/wiki/Seagram" title="Seagram">Seagram</a>. Named after the <a href="/wiki/Expo_67" title="Expo 67">Expo 67</a> <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s Fair">World\'s Fair</a>, the Expos\' initial home was <a href="/wiki/Jarry_Park_Stadium" title="Jarry Park Stadium">Jarry Park</a>. Managed by <a href="/wiki/Gene_Mauch" title="Gene Mauch">Gene Mauch</a>, the team lost 110 games in their first season, coincidentally matching the Padres inaugural win-loss record, and continued to struggle during their first decade with sub-.500 seasons.\n</p><p>Starting in 1977, the team\'s home venue was Montreal\'s <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Montreal)" title="Olympic Stadium (Montreal)">Olympic Stadium</a>, built for the <a href="/wiki/1976_Summer_Olympics" title="1976 Summer Olympics">1976 Summer Olympics</a>. Two years later, the team won a franchise-high 95 games, finishing second in the National League East. The Expos began the 1980s with a core group of young players, including catcher <a href="/wiki/Gary_Carter" title="Gary Carter">Gary Carter</a>, outfielders <a href="/wiki/Tim_Raines" title="Tim Raines">Tim Raines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andre_Dawson" title="Andre Dawson">Andre Dawson</a>, third baseman <a href="/wiki/Tim_Wallach" title="Tim Wallach">Tim Wallach</a>, and pitchers <a href="/wiki/Steve_Rogers_(baseball)" title="Steve Rogers (baseball)">Steve Rogers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gullickson" title="Bill Gullickson">Bill Gullickson</a>. The team won its only division championship in the strike-shortened split season of 1981, ending its season with a three games to two loss to the <a href="/wiki/1981_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1981 Los Angeles Dodgers season">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1981_National_League_Championship_Series" title="1981 National League Championship Series">National League Championship Series</a>.\n</p><p>The team spent most of the 1980s in the middle of the NL East pack, finishing in third or fourth place in eight out of nine seasons from 1982 to 1990. <a href="/wiki/Buck_Rodgers" title="Buck Rodgers">Buck Rodgers</a> was hired as manager before the 1985 season and guided the Expos to a .500 or better record five times in six years, with the highlight coming in 1987, when they won 91 games. They finished third, but were just four games behind the division-winning <a href="/wiki/1987_St._Louis_Cardinals" class="mw-redirect" title="1987 St. Louis Cardinals">Cardinals</a>.\n</p><p>Bronfman sold the team to a consortium of owners in 1991, with <a href="/wiki/Claude_Brochu" title="Claude Brochu">Claude Brochu</a> as the managing general partner.<sup id="cite_ref-ExposGuide1996_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ExposGuide1996-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-1991June-Gazette_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1991June-Gazette-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\nRodgers, at that time second only to Gene Mauch in number of Expos games managed, was replaced partway through the 1991 season. In May 1992, <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Alou" title="Felipe Alou">Felipe Alou</a>, a member of the Expos organization since 1976, was promoted to manager, becoming the first Dominican-born manager in MLB history.<sup id="cite_ref-ExposGuide1996_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ExposGuide1996-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Alou would become the leader in Expos games managed, while guiding the team to winning records, including 1994, when the Expos, led by a talented group of players including <a href="/wiki/Larry_Walker" title="Larry Walker">Larry Walker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mois%C3%A9s_Alou" title="Mois\xc3\xa9s Alou">Mois\xc3\xa9s Alou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marquis_Grissom" title="Marquis Grissom">Marquis Grissom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Pedro Mart\xc3\xadnez">Pedro Mart\xc3\xadnez</a>, had the best record in the major leagues until the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1994\xe2\x80\x9395 Major League Baseball strike">1994\xe2\x80\x9395 Major League Baseball strike</a> forced the cancellation of the remainder of the season. After the disappointment of 1994, Expos management began shedding its key players, and the team\'s fan support dwindled.\n</p><p>Brochu sold control of the team to <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Loria" title="Jeffrey Loria">Jeffrey Loria</a> in 1999,<sup id="cite_ref-ExposGuide2000_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ExposGuide2000-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GlobeAndMail-LoriaPurchase_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GlobeAndMail-LoriaPurchase-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\nbut Loria failed to close on a plan to build a new downtown ballpark, and did not reach an agreement on television and English radio broadcast contracts for the 2000 season, reducing the team\'s media coverage.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Proposed_2001_contraction">Proposed 2001 contraction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Proposed 2001 contraction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>After the 2001 season, MLB considered revoking the team\'s franchise, along with either the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Minnesota Twins</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Devil_Rays" class="mw-redirect" title="Tampa Bay Devil Rays">Tampa Bay Devil Rays</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>  In November 2001, Major League Baseball\'s owners voted 28\xe2\x80\x932 to contract the league by two teams \xe2\x80\x94 according to various sources, the Expos and the Minnesota Twins, both of which reportedly voted against contraction.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN-contraction_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-contraction-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\nSubsequently, the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> were sold to a partnership led by <a href="/wiki/John_W._Henry" title="John W. Henry">John W. Henry</a>, owner of the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Marlins" class="mw-redirect" title="Florida Marlins">Florida Marlins</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN-contraction_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-contraction-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\nIn order to clear the way for Henry\'s group to assume ownership of the Red Sox, Henry sold the Marlins to Loria, and MLB purchased the Expos from Loria.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN-contraction_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-contraction-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\nHowever, the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Sports_Facilities_Commission" title="Metropolitan Sports Facilities Commission">Metropolitan Sports Facilities Commission</a>, operator of the <a href="/wiki/Hubert_H._Humphrey_Metrodome" title="Hubert H. Humphrey Metrodome">Metrodome</a>, won an injunction requiring the Twins to play there in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN-contraction_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-contraction-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Because MLB was unable to revoke the Twins franchise, it was compelled to keep both the Twins and Expos as part of the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_schedule" title="Major League Baseball schedule">regular season schedule</a>. In the collective bargaining agreement signed with the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Players_Association" title="Major League Baseball Players Association">Major League Baseball Players Association</a> (MLBPA) in August 2002, contraction was prohibited until the end of the contract in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> By that time, the Expos had become the Washington Nationals and the Twins had made sufficient progress towards the eventual building of a new <a href="/wiki/Target_Field" title="Target Field">baseball-specific stadium</a> that contraction was no longer on the agenda.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Creation_of_the_Washington_Nationals">Creation of the Washington Nationals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Creation of the Washington Nationals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>With contraction no longer an option for the immediate term, MLB began looking for a relocation site for the Expos. Some of the choices included <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_City" title="Oklahoma City">Oklahoma City</a>; Washington, D.C.; <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan, Puerto Rico</a>; <a href="/wiki/Monterrey,_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Monterrey, Mexico">Monterrey, Mexico</a>; <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland, Oregon</a>; somewhere in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia" title="Northern Virginia">Northern Virginia</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Arlington,_Virginia" class="mw-redirect" title="Arlington, Virginia">Arlington</a> or <a href="/wiki/Dulles,_Virginia" title="Dulles, Virginia">Dulles</a>; <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">Norfolk, Virginia</a>; <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte, North Carolina</a>. <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> emerged as the front runners.\n</p><p>In both 2003 and 2004, the Expos played 22 of their home games in <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan, Puerto Rico</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Hiram_Bithorn_Stadium" title="Hiram Bithorn Stadium">Hiram Bithorn Stadium</a>, and the remaining 59 in Montreal.\n</p><p>On September 29, 2004, MLB announced that the Expos would move to Washington, D.C. in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-Myles-Gazette-2004-09-30_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Myles-Gazette-2004-09-30-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Expos played their final game on October 3 at <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a>, losing by a score of 8\xe2\x80\x931 against the <a href="/wiki/2004_New_York_Mets_season" title="2004 New York Mets season">New York Mets</a>, the same opponent that the Expos first faced at its start, 35 years earlier. On November 15, a lawsuit by the former team owners against MLB and former majority owner Jeffrey Loria was struck down by arbitrators, bringing to an end all legal actions that would impede a move. The owners of the other MLB teams approved the move to Washington in a 28\xe2\x80\x931 vote on December 3 (<a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a> owner <a href="/wiki/Peter_Angelos" title="Peter Angelos">Peter Angelos</a> cast the sole dissenting vote).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Washington_baseball_history_revived">Washington baseball history revived</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Washington baseball history revived">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Washington,_D.C._professional_baseball" title="History of Washington, D.C. professional baseball">History of Washington, D.C. professional baseball</a></div>\n<p>Numerous professional baseball teams have called Washington, D.C. home. The <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Washington_Senators_(1901%E2%80%9360)" title="History of the Washington Senators (1901\xe2\x80\x9360)">Washington Senators</a>, a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> (AL), played in the nation\'s capital from 1901 to 1960 before <a href="/wiki/Relocation_of_professional_sports_teams" title="Relocation of professional sports teams">moving</a> to Minnesota and becoming the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Twins</a>. The original Washington American League Base Ball Club was founded by three local businessmen: Edward J. Walsh, Benjamin Minor, and Harry Rapley.   <a href="/wiki/Clark_Griffith" title="Clark Griffith">Clark Griffith</a> was hired as manager in 1912 and became a part owner, accumulating majority shares in later years.  The stadium, originally known as National Park and then American League Park, later became known as <a href="/wiki/Griffith_Stadium" title="Griffith Stadium">Griffith Stadium</a>. With notable stars including <a href="/wiki/Walter_Johnson" title="Walter Johnson">Walter Johnson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Cronin" title="Joe Cronin">Joe Cronin</a>, the Senators won the <a href="/wiki/1924_World_Series" title="1924 World Series">1924 World Series</a> and pennants in <a href="/wiki/1925_World_Series" title="1925 World Series">1925</a> and <a href="/wiki/1933_World_Series" title="1933 World Series">1933</a>.  The franchise became more successful after moving to Minnesota for the 1961 season to be renamed the Minnesota Twins. A second <a href="/wiki/Washington_Senators_(1961%E2%80%9371)" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Senators (1961\xe2\x80\x9371)">Washington Senators</a> team (1961\xe2\x80\x931971) had a winning record only once in its 11 years, although it featured slugger <a href="/wiki/Frank_Howard_(baseball)" title="Frank Howard (baseball)">Frank Howard</a>, who was inducted into the Ring of Fame at the new Nationals Park in 2016.  This team was notable also because <a href="/wiki/Ted_Williams_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ted Williams (baseball)">Ted Williams</a> was manager in 1971.  The expansion Senators moved to Arlington, Texas for the 1972 season and changed its name to the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a>. The city of Washington spent the next 33 years without a baseball team.\n</p><p>Although there was some sentiment to revive the name Senators when the Montreal Expos franchise moved to Washington in 2005, legal and political considerations factored into the choice of Nationals, a revival of the first American League franchise\'s official name used from 1901 to 1956.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Politicians and others in the District of Columbia objected to the name Senators because the District of Columbia does not have <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia_voting_rights" title="District of Columbia voting rights">voting representation in Congress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In addition, the Rangers still owned the rights to the Senators name,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> although the Nationals were able to acquire the rights to the curly "W" logo from the Rangers.\n</p><p>Washington, D.C., mayor <a href="/wiki/Anthony_A._Williams" title="Anthony A. Williams">Anthony A. Williams</a> supported the name "Washington Grays", in honor of the Negro-league team the <a href="/wiki/Homestead_Grays" title="Homestead Grays">Homestead Grays</a> (1929\xe2\x80\x931950), which had been based in <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, but played many of their home games in Washington. In the end, the team owners chose the name "Washington Nationals".<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Washington_Nationals">Washington Nationals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Washington Nationals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Washington_Nationals" title="History of the Washington Nationals">History of the Washington Nationals</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nationals_Game_-_2009_-_Stierch.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Nationals_Game_-_2009_-_Stierch.jpg/220px-Nationals_Game_-_2009_-_Stierch.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Nationals_Game_-_2009_-_Stierch.jpg/330px-Nationals_Game_-_2009_-_Stierch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Nationals_Game_-_2009_-_Stierch.jpg/440px-Nationals_Game_-_2009_-_Stierch.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nationals_Game_-_2009_-_Stierch.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nationals versus the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a> in 2009 at <a href="/wiki/Nationals_Park" title="Nationals Park">Nationals Park</a></div></div></div>\n<p>When Ted Lerner took over the club in mid-2006, he hired <a href="/wiki/Stan_Kasten" title="Stan Kasten">Stan Kasten</a> as team president. Kasten was widely known as the architect of the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta Braves</a> before and during their run of 14 division titles. Kasten was also the general manager or president of many other <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>-area sports teams, including the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Hawks" title="Atlanta Hawks">Atlanta Hawks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Thrashers" title="Atlanta Thrashers">Atlanta Thrashers</a>. "The Plan", as it became known, was a long-range rebuilding and restructuring of the team from the ground up. This plan included investing in the farm system and the draft, and having a suitable team to go along with their new stadium.\n</p><p>In the front office, the Nationals hired the well-respected former Arizona scouting director <a href="/wiki/Mike_Rizzo_(baseball)" title="Mike Rizzo (baseball)">Mike Rizzo</a> to be the vice president of baseball operations, second in charge under then-general manager Jim Bowden.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Thanks to back-to-back No. 1 picks of <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Strasburg" title="Stephen Strasburg">Stephen Strasburg</a> (in <a href="/wiki/2009_Major_League_Baseball_draft" title="2009 Major League Baseball draft">2009</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Bryce_Harper" title="Bryce Harper">Bryce Harper</a> (in <a href="/wiki/2010_Major_League_Baseball_draft" title="2010 Major League Baseball draft">2010</a>), and other strong moves to their farm system, the Nationals became a contending team by 2012, winning division titles in 2012, 2014, 2016, and 2017, but have lost in NLDS each time.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In April 2015, Commissioner Rob Manfred announced that Nationals Park was selected by Major League Baseball to host the 2018 All Star Game.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2016, the Nationals acquired Mets infielder <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Murphy_(baseball)" title="Daniel Murphy (baseball)">Daniel Murphy</a>, who has made the All Star Game in each of his two years as a National.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On July 31, 2018, the Nationals set a scoring record with a 25-4 win over the <a href="/wiki/Mets" class="mw-redirect" title="Mets">Mets</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Postseason_appearances">Postseason appearances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Postseason appearances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Montreal Expos-Washington Nationals franchise is the only National League franchise and one of only two MLB franchises \xe2\x80\x93 with the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a>\xe2\x80\xb2s <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Seattle Mariners</a> \xe2\x80\x93 which has never reached the <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a>. Although the Expos won one postseason series - the <a href="/wiki/1981_National_League_Division_Series" title="1981 National League Division Series">1981 National League Division Series</a> \xe2\x80\x93 during their 36 seasons in Montreal, the Nationals have never won a postseason series since arriving in Washington in 2005 despite making four playoff appearances.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" cellspacing="2">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="background-color:#AA1E22;color:#FFFFFF;-moz-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #212759, inset -2px -2px 0 #212759; -webkit-box-shadow: inset 2px Frick Award</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Ford C. Frick Award">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="toccolours" style="font-size: 95%; margin: 1em auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="background-color: #AA1E22; color: #FFFFFF; text-align: center;">Washington Nationals <a href="/wiki/Ford_C._Frick_Award" title="Ford C. Museum\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>\n<table style="margin: 1em auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Tom_Cheek" title="Tom Cheek">Tom Cheek</a>\n</p>\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n<p><b><a href="/wiki/Dave_Van_Horne" title="Dave Van Horne">Dave Van Horne</a></b>\n</p>\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="plainlist">\n<ul><li><b>Names in bold</b> received the award based primarily on their work as broadcasters for the Expos or Nationals.</li>\n<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>\n<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>\n<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>\n<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li></ul>\n</div>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retired_numbers">Retired numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Retired numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="font-style:bold; font-size:120%; border:3px;">\n\n<tbody><tr style="text-align:center; background:#0c2d83;">\n<td><a href="/wiki/File:NatsRetired42.png" class="image"><img alt="NatsRetired42.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/NatsRetired42.png/95px-NatsRetired42.png" width="95" height="95" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/NatsRetired42.png/143px-NatsRetired42.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/NatsRetired42.png/190px-NatsRetired42.png 2x" data-file-width="576" data-file-height="576" /></a><span style="color:#fff;"><br /><b><a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson"><span style="color:#fff;">Jackie<br />Robinson</span></a></b><br />2B<br /><span style="font-size:87%;">Retired 1997</span></span>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_retired_numbers" title="List of Major League Baseball retired numbers">List of Major League Baseball retired numbers</a></div>\n<p>During the franchise\'s period in Montreal, the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Expos#Retired_numbers" title="Montreal Expos">Montreal Expos retired three numbers</a> in honor of four players, plus <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a>\'s number 42 which was retired throughout all Major League Baseball in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-WashingtonRetiredNumbers_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashingtonRetiredNumbers-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\nFollowing the move to Washington, D.C., the numbers (except 42) were returned to circulation and remain in use as of  2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, although the "Team History" section of the Nationals\' website continues to refer to the numbers as "retired."<sup id="cite_ref-WashingtonRetiredNumbers_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashingtonRetiredNumbers-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> After the Expos\' departure from Montreal, the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>\xe2\x80\xb2s <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Canadiens" title="Montreal Canadiens">Montreal Canadiens</a> hung a banner in <a href="/wiki/Bell_Centre" title="Bell Centre">Bell Centre</a> honoring the Expos\' retired numbers.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ring_of_Honor">Ring of Honor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ring of Honor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On August 10, 2010, the Nationals unveiled a "Ring of Honor"<sup id="cite_ref-hallofstars_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hallofstars-46">&#91;note 3&#93;</a></sup> at Nationals Park to honor <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">National Baseball Hall of Fame</a> members who had played "significant years" for the Washington Nationals, original Washington Senators (1901\xe2\x80\x931960), expansion Washington Senators (1961\xe2\x80\x931971), Homestead Grays, or Montreal Expos.<sup id="cite_ref-2010pressrelease_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010pressrelease-47">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-steinberg20160826_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20160826-48">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> In late August 2016, the team dropped the criterion that an inductee be a member of the National Baseball Hall of Fame, also opening membership to "anyone who has made a significant contribution to the game of baseball in Washington, D.C.";<sup id="cite_ref-steinberg20160826_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20160826-48">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> the first inductee under the revised criteria was <a href="/wiki/Frank_Howard_(baseball)" title="Frank Howard (baseball)">Frank Howard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-steinberg20160826_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20160826-48">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Nationals\xe2\x80\xb2 attempt to honor the Montreal-Washington franchise\xe2\x80\xb2s entire history in the Ring of Honor, as well as by tracking Montreal-Washington franchise records, is not without controversy; it has been criticized as "an embodiment of the team\xe2\x80\x99s desire to find history before it can make much."<sup id="cite_ref-janes20180908_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-janes20180908-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Although Nationals fans generally take little interest in the franchise\xe2\x80\xb2s Montreal years, some do appreciate acknowledging that the franchise has a history that predates its arrival in Washington, and former Expo <a href="/wiki/Tim_Raines" title="Tim Raines">Tim Raines</a> received a warm round of applause from fans at Nationals Park at his induction ceremony on August 28, 2017, even though he had never even visited Washington, D.C., before, let alone played baseball there.<sup id="cite_ref-janes20180908_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-janes20180908-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-steinberg20170830_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20170830-50">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Some Montreal Expos fans express appreciation that the Nationals are honoring the Expos, and Expos players inducted into the Ring of Honor have expressed gratitude that the Nationals chose to include them, especially with no MLB team in Montreal to honor their careers.<sup id="cite_ref-steinberg20170830_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20170830-50">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> However, few Nationals fans have taken an interest in franchise records, preferring to compare Nationals records with those of previous Washington MLB teams instead,<sup id="cite_ref-steinberg20170830_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20170830-50">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> and a segment of Nationals fans actively opposes the inclusion of Expos history into that of the Nationals, taking the view that the Montreal years are irrelevant to Washington and that the team made a complete break with its past and started anew when it arrived in Washington, inheriting the history of the two Washington Senators teams rather than that of the Expos.<sup id="cite_ref-steinberg20170830_50-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20170830-50">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, Montreal Expos fans have taken little or no interest in the achievements of Nationals players, and some Expos fans strongly oppose the inclusion of former Expos in the Ring, taking the position that to do so is to co-opt the history of the Expos, which they say belongs solely in Montreal.<sup id="cite_ref-steinberg20170830_50-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20170830-50">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Observers also have noted that the admission of the first Nationals player to the Ring of Honor, <a href="/wiki/Iv%C3%A1n_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Iv\xc3\xa1n Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Iv\xc3\xa1n "Pudge" Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-janes20180908_49-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-janes20180908-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> although well-liked as a National, highlights another awkward aspect of the Ring of Honor\'s acceptance criteria, because Rodriguez\'s inclusion arose out of his admission to the National Baseball Hall of Fame based on his exploits for other teams, not out of anything he did during a 155-game, two-season stint with the Nationals at the end of his career in years in which the Nationals posted mediocre records. Nationals general manager <a href="/wiki/Mike_Rizzo" title="Mike Rizzo">Mike Rizzo</a> responded that his inclusion had merit even based on his time with the Nationals, when he "taught us how to be a professional franchise."<sup id="cite_ref-janes20180908_49-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-janes20180908-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In a ceremony held at Nationals Park between games of a doubleheader on the evening of September 8, 2018, the Nationals inducted former outfielder <a href="/wiki/Jayson_Werth" title="Jayson Werth">Jayson Werth</a>, who played for the Nationals from <a href="/wiki/2011_Washington_Nationals_season" title="2011 Washington Nationals season">2011</a> through <a href="/wiki/2017_Washington_Nationals_season" title="2017 Washington Nationals season">2017</a>, into the Ring of Honor.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> He became the first "true" National<sup id="cite_ref-janes20180908_49-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-janes20180908-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> \xe2\x80\x93 the first person based specifically on his career as a National \xe2\x80\x93 inducted into the Ring of Honor.<sup id="cite_ref-janes20180908_49-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-janes20180908-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Ring of Honor includes:<sup id="cite_ref-2010pressrelease_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010pressrelease-47">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-steinberg20160826_48-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20160826-48">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Prominent fans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rubber_Chicken_Man_with_baseball_writer_Paul_Dickson.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Rubber_Chicken_Man_with_baseball_writer_Paul_Dickson.jpg/220px-Rubber_Chicken_Man_with_baseball_writer_Paul_Dickson.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Rubber_Chicken_Man_with_baseball_writer_Paul_Dickson.jpg/330px-Rubber_Chicken_Man_with_baseball_writer_Paul_Dickson.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Rubber_Chicken_Man_with_baseball_writer_Paul_Dickson.jpg/440px-Rubber_Chicken_Man_with_baseball_writer_Paul_Dickson.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="2432" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rubber_Chicken_Man_with_baseball_writer_Paul_Dickson.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Rubber Chicken Man" Hugh Kaufman cheers on the Washington Nationals with baseball writer <a href="/wiki/Paul_Dickson_(writer)" title="Paul Dickson (writer)">Paul Dickson</a>. Kaufman waves a rubber chicken over the Nats\' dugout to ward off bad luck, and sometimes ritually "sacrifices" them to improve team performance.</div></div></div><p>One prominent fan is "<a href="/wiki/Rubber_Chicken_Man" title="Rubber Chicken Man">Rubber Chicken Man</a>" Hugh Kaufman, who waves a rubber chicken over the dugout to ward off "<a href="/wiki/JuJu" class="mw-redirect" title="JuJu">JuJu</a>". Local sports writers have noted that his ritual "sacrifices" of rubber chickens often precede turnarounds in the Nationals\' performance.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Kaufman has built a following at the Stadium and in 2013 started a group called the "Secret Society of the Rubber Chicken" that now claims several Nationals players among its members.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_standings">Season standings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Season season">2018</a>\n</td>\n<td>NL\n</td>\n<td>East\n</td>\n<td>2nd\n</td>\n<td>82\n</td>\n<td>80\n</td>\n<td>.506\n</td>\n<td>8\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x94\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/2019_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2019 Major League Baseball season">2019</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/2019_Washington_Nationals_season" title="2019 Washington Nationals season">2019</a>\n</td>\n<td>NL\n</td>\n<td>East\n</td>\n<td colspan="7">Season scheduled for March 28\xe2\x80\x93September 29, 2019.\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table><p><b>Bold</b> denotes a playoff season, pennant or championship; <i>italics</i> denote an active season.\n</p><h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Spring_training">Spring training</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Spring training">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Space_Coast_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Space Coast Stadium">Space Coast Stadium</a> and <a href="/wiki/FITTEAM_Ballpark_of_the_Palm_Beaches" title="FITTEAM Ballpark of the Palm Beaches">FITTEAM Ballpark of the Palm Beaches</a></div>\n<p>The Nationals hold spring training in <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, where they play their annual slate of <a href="/wiki/Grapefruit_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Grapefruit League">Grapefruit League</a> games. From 2005 through 2016, they held spring training at <a href="/wiki/Space_Coast_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Space Coast Stadium">Space Coast Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Viera,_Florida" title="Viera, Florida">Viera</a>, Florida, a facility that they inherited from the Expos. In 2017, the Nationals moved their spring training operations to The Ballpark of the Palm Beaches, a new facility they share with the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="West Palm Beach, Florida">West Palm Beach</a>, Florida; they played their first Grapefruit League game there on February 28, 2017. On February 16, 2018, it was renamed <a href="/wiki/FITTEAM_Ballpark_of_the_Palm_Beaches" title="FITTEAM Ballpark of the Palm Beaches">FITTEAM Ballpark of the Palm Beaches</a> after the Nationals and Astros signed a 12-year deal for the naming rights to the stadium that day with FITTEAM, an event brand partnership and <a href="/wiki/Organic_products" class="mw-redirect" title="Organic products">organic products</a> firm located in Palm Beach Gardens, Florida.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Minor_league_affiliations">Minor league affiliations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Minor league affiliations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Washington_Nationals_minor_league_affiliates" title="List of Washington Nationals minor league affiliates">List of Washington Nationals minor league affiliates</a></div>\n<p>On September 18, 2018, the Nationals and the <a href="/wiki/Fresno_Grizzlies" title="Fresno Grizzlies">Fresno Grizzlies</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_League" title="Pacific Coast League">Pacific Coast League</a> announced that they had stuck a two-year player-development deal that make Fresno the Nationals\' <a href="/wiki/Triple-A_(baseball)" title="Triple-A (baseball)">Class AAA</a> affiliate beginning in the <a href="/wiki/2019_Washington_Nationals_season" title="2019 Washington Nationals season">2019 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="text-align:center; Expos">Watertown Expos</a> (1970\xe2\x80\x931971)\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nationals_Dream_Foundation">Nationals Dream Foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Nationals Dream Foundation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Washington Nationals Dream Foundation is the team\'s charity which is "committed to community partnerships that improve the lives of children and families across the Washington Capital Region. The foundation opened a youth baseball academy in partnership with the D.C. government,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> and a pediatric <a href="/wiki/Diabetes" class="mw-redirect" title="Diabetes">diabetes</a> care center at <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_National_Medical_Center" title="Children&#39;s National Medical Center">Children\'s National Medical Center</a> in partnership with the Center. The foundation also provides grants to local organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On August 1, 2011, the foundation, in partnership with several local organizations, formally opened Miracle Field in <a href="/wiki/Germantown,_Maryland" title="Germantown, Maryland">Germantown, Maryland</a> as part of an effort to encourage athletic activity in children with "mental and/or physical challenges."<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> According to Steven Miller of MLB.com, what sets Miracle Field apart in terms of safety is its unique design, as it "is made entirely of a cushioned synthetic turf that is five-eighths of an inch thick-- providing a safe surface for children in wheelchairs or with other handicaps." <sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_and_television">Radio and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Radio and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals_Radio_Network" title="Washington Nationals Radio Network">Washington Nationals Radio Network</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nationals_Presidents.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Nationals_Presidents.jpg/225px-Nationals_Presidents.jpg" width="225" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Nationals_Presidents.jpg/338px-Nationals_Presidents.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Nationals_Presidents.jpg/450px-Nationals_Presidents.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3072" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nationals_Presidents.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mascots dressed as <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> in the stands during a 2010 game against the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a>. They compete in the <a href="/wiki/Presidents_Race" title="Presidents Race">Presidents Race</a> every mid-fourth inning of a home game.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Nationals\' <a href="/wiki/Flagship" title="Flagship">flagship</a> <a href="/wiki/Radio_station" title="Radio station">radio station</a> is <a href="/wiki/WJFK-FM" title="WJFK-FM">WJFK-FM</a> (106.7 FM) "The Fan", which is owned by <a href="/wiki/Entercom" title="Entercom">Entercom</a>. <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Slowes" title="Charlie Slowes">Charlie Slowes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dave_Jageler" title="Dave Jageler">Dave Jageler</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Play-by-play" class="mw-redirect" title="Play-by-play">play-by-play</a> announcers. WJFK fronts a <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals_Radio_Network" title="Washington Nationals Radio Network">radio network</a> of 19  stations serving portions of <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a> as well as the District.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/WFED" title="WFED">WFED</a> (1500 AM) had been the flagship station since the 2006 season until a multi-year agreement was reached between the Nationals and WJFK before the 2011 season. WFED remains on the network as an affiliate; its 50 kilowatt <a href="/wiki/Clear-channel_station" title="Clear-channel station">clear-channel</a> signal allows the Nationals\' home-team call to be heard up and down the East Coast.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/WWZZ" title="WWZZ">WWZZ</a> (104.1 FM), which carried games in the 2005 season, was the team\'s first flagship radio station.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_Sports_Network" title="Mid-Atlantic Sports Network">Mid-Atlantic Sports Network</a> (MASN) televises all games not picked up by one of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_television" title="Major League Baseball on television">MLB\'s national television partners</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bob_Carpenter_(sportscaster)" title="Bob Carpenter (sportscaster)">Bob Carpenter</a> has been the TV play-by-play announcer since 2006 and <a href="/wiki/F.P._Santangelo" class="mw-redirect" title="F.P. Santangelo">F.P. Santangelo</a> was hired in January 2011 as <a href="/wiki/Color_analyst" class="mw-redirect" title="Color analyst">color analyst</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-coloranalyst_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coloranalyst-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mel_Proctor" title="Mel Proctor">Mel Proctor</a> was the TV play-by-announcer in 2005, and former color analysts are <a href="/wiki/Ron_Darling" title="Ron Darling">Ron Darling</a> (2005), <a href="/wiki/Tom_Paciorek" title="Tom Paciorek">Tom Paciorek</a> (2006), <a href="/wiki/Don_Sutton" title="Don Sutton">Don Sutton</a> (2007\xe2\x80\x932008), and <a href="/wiki/Rob_Dibble" title="Rob Dibble">Rob Dibble</a>, who took over the job in 2009 and was fired in September 2010 after criticizing Stephen Strasburg for not pitching while injured. <a href="/wiki/Ray_Knight" title="Ray Knight">Ray Knight</a> filled in as color analyst in September 2010 after Dibble was fired.<sup id="cite_ref-coloranalyst_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coloranalyst-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n<sup id="cite_ref-coloranalyst_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coloranalyst-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Previously, <a href="/wiki/WDCA" title="WDCA">WDCA</a> (channel 20) carried 76 games in the 2005 season while the newly founded MASN was still negotiating cable carriage.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> From 2009 through 2017, MASN syndicated a package of 20 games for simulcast on an over-the-air television station in Washington. Broadcast partners under this arrangement were <a href="/wiki/WDCW" title="WDCW">WDCW</a> (channel 50) from 2009 through 2012 and <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/WUSA_(TV)" title="WUSA (TV)">WUSA</a> (channel 9) from 2013 through 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> MASN did not continue the syndication deal for the 2018 season.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the midst of a season in which they finished with the worst record in Major League Baseball, the Nationals\xe2\x80\xb2 television ratings were among the worst in the National League in July 2008<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> but increased during the 2010 and 2011 seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Since 2012, when they began to achieve consistent success on the field, their television viewership has grown continually and dramatically. By 2016, the Nationals\xe2\x80\xb2 prime-time television ratings were 15th highest among the 29 U.S. MLB teams, and they rose to 12th in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="Baltimore_Orioles_.28Beltway_Series.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Baltimore_Orioles_(Beltway_Series)">Baltimore Orioles (Beltway Series)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Baltimore Orioles (Beltway Series)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Beltway_Series" title="Beltway Series">Beltway Series</a></div>\n<p>The Nationals have an <a href="/wiki/Interleague_play" title="Interleague play">interleague</a> <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_rivalries" title="Major League Baseball rivalries">rivalry</a> with the nearby <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a>, which is nicknamed the <a href="/wiki/Beltway_Series" title="Beltway Series">Beltway Series</a>. The teams have played two series a season \xe2\x80\x93 one in Baltimore and one in Washington \xe2\x80\x93 since <a href="/wiki/2006_Washington_Nationals_season" title="2006 Washington Nationals season">2006</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> They were: the Washington Olympics for 41 games in 1871-1872,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> the Washington Nationals for 11 games in 1872,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> the Washington Blue Legs for 39 games in 1873,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and a different Washington Nationals franchise for 28 games in 1875.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-2011finish-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-2011finish_44-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-2011finish_44-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">During <a href="/wiki/2011_Washington_Nationals_season" title="2011 Washington Nationals season">2011</a>, Riggleman and McLaren combined with <a href="/wiki/Davey_Johnson" title="Davey Johnson">Davey Johnson</a> for an 80-81 (.497), third-place finish. Riggleman\xe2\x80\xb2s record in 2011 was 38\xe2\x80\x9337 (.507), McLaren\xe2\x80\xb2s was 2\xe2\x80\x931 (.667), and Johnson\xe2\x80\xb2s was 40\xe2\x80\x9343 (.482).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-hallofstars-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-hallofstars_46-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Ring of Honor should not be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Hall_of_Stars" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Hall of Stars">Washington Hall of Stars</a>.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Footnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div style="font-size: 100%">\n<ol><li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_stadiuma"><a href="#ref_stadiuma"><b><sup>a</sup></b></a></span> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.dcsec.com/rfk_stadium/fast_facts.asp">RFK Stadium Fast Facts</a></li></ol>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_Nationals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em;
